Method of Learning
intermediate
6 min
The Quranic Basis for Rational Arguments
Buti enumerates Quranic commands and arguments that support rational kalam methodology.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Buti grounds the kalam methodology in specific Quranic commands and arguments.

Core Idea
The kalam method is not un-Quranic; the Quran itself commands reason and uses rational proofs.

Buti continues his defense by arguing that the rational method is not only necessary for non-believers but is actually rooted in the Quran. He cites several Quranic principles and arguments that demonstrate the compatibility of rational theology with divine revelation.

Guided Path
1
Read the futility statements
Notice Buti's strong language: 'It is futile' to use Quranic verses with those who don't accept the Quran. This underscores the need for a different approach.
2
Identify the Quranic commands
Buti mentions two commands: not to follow without knowledge, and to use reason. Find these in the passage.
3
Recognize the Quranic arguments
Buti lists specific rational proofs used in the Quran: teleological cause, mutual hindrance, circularity, and preponderance. See how each is rooted in Quranic verses.
4
Understand the conclusion
Buti asks rhetorically what more one could want from the Quran to prove that rational debate is part of its methodology.

فهل أسأت فيها أقدمت عليه من تأليف هذا الكتاب ..؟ وهل كان يسعني ـ في مجال الكشف عن حقائق الإيمان بالله عز وجل أمام أصحاب الشكوك والشبهات المختلفة - أن لا أناقشهم على أسس منطقية عامة يفهمونها ويؤمنون بها ؟. ويتحدث البعض عن منهج القرآن .. وضرورة الاستعاضة عن هذا كله بمنهج القرآن .. ونحن نقول لهؤلاء الإخوة : لاتنافي بين المنهجين ولا تعطيل لأحدهما على حساب الآخر. فنحن بحاجة إلى عرض منهج القرآن بالنسبة لمن تركزت في قلبه مبادئ الإيمان بالله ورسوله . ولكنه لا يزال بحاجة إلى تقويتها والحفاظ عليها وإقامة الصورة الإسلامية الصحيحة في فكره دون أي زيف أو انحراف عنها . ونحن ننصح لمثل هذا الإنسان بعدم إضاعة الوقت في تأمل هذه المناقشات الفكرية ، التي تحوم حول البحث في شبهات ماهو منها في شيء ، إلا أن يحتاج إليها في مجال توجيه الآخرين وتعليمهم. ولكنا بحاجة إلى المنهج المنطقي والفكري العام الذي سلكه علماء الكلام ، بالنسبة لمن لم يدخل بفكره بعد في دائرة الإيمان بالله ورسوله والكتاب الذي نزل على رسوله إن من العبث أن تعرض أمام هؤلاء آيات القرآن وعظاته وهو لم يؤمن بعد بهذا الذي تسميه قرآناً .. وإن من العبث أن تعمد إلى من استحكمت في فكره شبهة من هذه الشبه العلمية التي كنا نبحث فيها آنفاً ، فتعالجها بهذا الذي يفهمه البعض من معنى منهج القرآن وأقول : بهذا الذي يفهمه البعض .. ولا أقول : منهج القرآن ، لأن المنهج الذي سار عليه أكثر علماء الكلام في عصورهم ونسير نحن عليه في مثل هذا الكتاب ليس خارجاً على منهج القرآن . فالقرآن أمرنا أن لا نقفو في أفكارنا واعتقادنا مالا علم لنا به . وأمرنا أن نحكم العقل وموازينه في كل ما يعرض لنا من أمور الحياة . والقرآن ناقش المشركين طبقاً لميزان العلة الغائية » المائلة في الكون. والقرآن نبه أفكار المشركين إلى بطلان الشريك الله تعالى طبقاً لما يقتضيه برهان « التمانع » كما نبه إلى ضرورة وجود الله عز وجل استدلالاً بقانون بطلان الدور وقانون بطلان الرجحان بدون مرجح (۱) فأي دستور تريده من القرآن أكثر من هذا ، كي تطمئن إلى أن مناقشة أصحاب الشبهات طبقاً لمقتضى الأدلة والبراهين التي يتعاملون بها هو من صميم المنهج القرآني ؟! ولا يعنيني ، إذا كان كلامي صحيحاً، أن يأتي مخالفاً لما يراه بعض المفكرين أو المخلصين في دعوتهم إلى الإسلام . فليس شرطاً لعظمة الدعاة إلى الله تعالى وعلو شأنهم وإشراق أفكارهم أن لا يخطئوا في مسألة ما ، أو أن لا يخونهم البحث في تقديرها حق قدرهـا من سائر الجوانب. إن هذا الشرط لو كان صحيحاً ، فإنما هو يعني العصمة إذا .. وليس من أحد بعـد رسول الله لا يوصف بالعصمة. تلك هي خلاصة الأفكار والملاحظات التي أحببت أن أثبتها في هذه المقدمة . وأسأل الله تعالى أن لا يكلني إلى نفسي في شيء مما أفعله أو أكتبه أو أقوله ، وأن لا يجعل حظي من هذا الكتاب ما يحبط المثوبة عليه يوم القيامة ، وأن يتغمدني برحمته وينفعني بـدعـاء الصالحين لي في ظهر الغيب . حرر في شعبان ۱۳۹۰ الموافق لتشرين الثاني ۱۹۷۰ محمد سعيد رمضان البوطي (۱) برهان التمانع تجده في قوله عز وحل : * لو كان فيها الهة إلا اللهُ لَفَسَدَتا ) وبرهان ظاهرة العلـة الغـائيـة واصح [؟] برهان بطلاب الرححان بدون مرحح وبطلان الدور تقرؤه في قوله تعالى : في أم خُلقوا من غير شَيءٍ أمْ هُمُ الخالقُونَ . أم خَلَقُوا السَّموات والأرض بَل لا يُوقنون ) .
Did I then do wrong in undertaking the composition of this book? And would it have been possible for me – in the field of revealing the truths of faith in Allah Almighty before those who harbor doubts and various suspicions – not to debate them on general logical foundations that they understand and believe in? Some speak about the methodology of the Quran and the necessity of substituting all this with the methodology of the Quran. And we say to these brothers: there is no contradiction between the two methodologies, nor any neglect of one at the expense of the other. For we need to present the methodology of the Quran for one whose heart is already grounded in the principles of faith in Allah and His Messenger, but still needs to strengthen them, preserve them, and establish a correct Islamic picture in his mind without any falsehood or deviation from it. And we advise such a person not to waste time pondering these intellectual discussions that revolve around the investigation of doubts that are nothing to him, unless he needs them for the purpose of guiding and teaching others. But we need the general logical and intellectual methodology that the theologians (ulama al-kalam) have followed, for one whose mind has not yet entered the circle of faith in Allah and His Messenger and the Book that was revealed to His Messenger. It is futile to present before these people the verses of the Quran and its exhortations while he has not yet believed in that which you call a Quran... And it is futile to approach one whose mind has become entrenched with one of these scientific doubts that we were discussing earlier, and treat it with what some people understand by 'the methodology of the Quran' – and I say: with what some people understand, and I do not say: the methodology of the Quran, because the methodology that most theologians followed in their times and that we follow in such a book is not outside the methodology of the Quran. ?

?

?

Defending the Method and Acknowledging Human Fallibility
Buti defends his methodology, asserts human fallibility, and concludes with a prayer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Buti's humble conclusion, where he defends his method against criticism and affirms that only the Prophet is infallible.

Core Idea
Truth is not determined by agreement; no scholar after the Prophet is infallible.

In his concluding remarks, Buti addresses potential objections to his approach. He emphasizes that being correct is more important than conforming to popular opinions, and that human scholars—no matter how great—are fallible. He ends with a prayer for divine mercy and acceptance.

Guided Path
1
Read the defense against critics
Buti states that it does not concern him if his views contradict some thinkers, provided his speech is correct.
2
Understand the infallibility argument
Buti argues that requiring scholars to never err would be claiming infallibility, which belongs only to the Prophet.
3
Notice the prayer and humility
Buti ends with a supplication, asking Allah not to entrust him to himself and to accept his work. This shows his humility.
4
Review the footnote references
The footnote connects the rational proofs mentioned earlier to specific Quranic verses, grounding them in revelation.

ولا يعنيني ، إذا كان كلامي صحيحاً، أن يأتي مخالفاً لما يراه بعض المفكرين أو المخلصين في دعوتهم إلى الإسلام . فليس شرطاً لعظمة الدعاة إلى الله تعالى وعلو شأنهم وإشراق أفكارهم أن لا يخطئوا في مسألة ما ، أو أن لا يخونهم البحث في تقديرها حق قدرهـا من سائر الجوانب. إن هذا الشرط لو كان صحيحاً ، فإنما هو يعني العصمة إذا .. وليس من أحد بعـد رسول الله لا يوصف بالعصمة. تلك هي خلاصة الأفكار والملاحظات التي أحببت أن أثبتها في هذه المقدمة . وأسأل الله تعالى أن لا يكلني إلى نفسي في شيء مما أفعله أو أكتبه أو أقوله ، وأن لا يجعل حظي من هذا الكتاب ما يحبط المثوبة عليه يوم القيامة ، وأن يتغمدني برحمته وينفعني بـدعـاء الصالحين لي في ظهر الغيب . حرر في شعبان ۱۳۹۰ الموافق لتشرين الثاني ۱۹۷۰ محمد سعيد رمضان البوطي (۱) برهان التمانع تجده في قوله عز وحل : * لو كان فيها الهة إلا اللهُ لَفَسَدَتا ) وبرهان ظاهرة العلـة الغـائيـة واصح [؟] برهان بطلاب الرححان بدون مرحح وبطلان الدور تقرؤه في قوله تعالى : في أم خُلقوا من غير شَيءٍ أمْ هُمُ الخالقُونَ . أم خَلَقُوا السَّموات والأرض بَل لا يُوقنون ) .
Did I then do wrong in undertaking the composition of this book? And would it have been possible for me – in the field of revealing the truths of faith in Allah Almighty before those who harbor doubts and various suspicions – not to debate them on general logical foundations that they understand and believe in? Some speak about the methodology of the Quran and the necessity of substituting all this with the methodology of the Quran. And we say to these brothers: there is no contradiction between the two methodologies, nor any neglect of one at the expense of the other. For we need to present the methodology of the Quran for one whose heart is already grounded in the principles of faith in Allah and His Messenger, but still needs to strengthen them, preserve them, and establish a correct Islamic picture in his mind without any falsehood or deviation from it. And we advise such a person not to waste time pondering these intellectual discussions that revolve around the investigation of doubts that are nothing to him, unless he needs them for the purpose of guiding and teaching others. But we need the general logical and intellectual methodology that the theologians (ulama al-kalam) have followed, for one whose mind has not yet entered the circle of faith in Allah and His Messenger and the Book that was revealed to His Messenger. It is futile to present before these people the verses of the Quran and its exhortations while he has not yet believed in that which you call a Quran... And it is futile to approach one whose mind has become entrenched with one of these scientific doubts that we were discussing earlier, and treat it with what some people understand by 'the methodology of the Quran' – and I say: with what some people understand, and I do not say: the methodology of the Quran, because the methodology that most theologians followed in their times and that we follow in such a book is not outside the methodology of the Quran. For the Quran commanded us not to follow in our thoughts and beliefs that of which we have no knowledge. And it commanded us to judge by reason and its scales in every matter of life that comes to us. And the Quran debated the polytheists according to the scale of the teleological cause (*al-illa al-gha'iyya*) manifest in the universe. And the Quran alerted the minds of the polytheists to the invalidity of a partner with Allah Almighty according to what is required by the proof of mutual hindrance (*burhan al-tamanu'*), just as it alerted to the necessity of the existence of Allah Almighty by inferring from the law of the invalidity of circularity (*qanun butlan al-dawr*) and the law of the invalidity of preponderance without a preponderater (*qanun butlan al-tarjih bila murajjih*). So what constitution do you want from the Quran more than this, to reassure you that debating the people of doubts according to the requirements of the proofs and evidences they deal with is from the core of the Quranic methodology? And it does not concern me, if my speech is correct, that it may contradict what some thinkers or sincere people in their call to Islam see. For it is not a condition for the greatness of the callers to Allah Almighty, their high standing, and the brightness of their ideas that they never err in some matter, or that research never fails them in assessing it its proper due from all aspects. If this condition were true, it would mean infallibility... And there is none after the Messenger of Allah who is described as infallible. Those are the summary of the ideas and observations that I wished to record in this introduction. And I ask Allah Almighty not to entrust me to myself in anything I do, write, or say, and not to make my share from this book of that which voids the reward for it on the Day of Resurrection, and to envelop me with His mercy and benefit me through the prayers of the righteous for me in the unseen. Written in Sha'ban 1390 AH, corresponding to November 1970. Muhammad Sa'id Ramadan al-Buti. (1) The proof of mutual hindrance is found in His saying, Mighty and Sublime: {If there were in them [the heavens and earth] gods besides Allah, they would both have been corrupted.} And the proof of the teleological phenomenon and... [?] The proof of the invalidity of preponderance without a preponderater and the invalidity of circularity is read in His saying, Exalted: {Or were they created of nothing, or are they the creators? Or did they create the heavens and the earth? Rather, they are not certain.}
Source pages p. 19

Commentary
This passage is a defense of the kalam methodology, written in the introduction of the book. The author, Ramadan al-Buti, begins by asking rhetorically whether he did wrong in writing this book and whether he could have avoided debating doubters on logical foundations they accept. He then addresses critics who advocate for exclusively using the Quranic method in da'wah. Buti asserts that there is no contradiction between the two methods; each serves a different purpose. For believers already grounded in faith, the Quranic method of exhortation is sufficient. However, for those not yet convinced of the Quran's divine authority, it is futile to present Quranic verses as proof, because they do not yet accept the Quran as revelation. For such people, a rational, logical methodology—the one employed by classical theologians (ulama al-kalam)—is necessary. Buti then demonstrates that this logical methodology is not alien to the Quran itself. He cites several Quranic commands and examples: the Quran forbids following what one has no knowledge of, commands the use of reason, and debates polytheists using rational arguments such as the teleological argument (the order in the universe pointing to a Creator), the argument of mutual hindrance (two gods would cause corruption), the argument against circularity (rejecting infinite regress), and the argument of preponderance without a preponderater (every contingent thing requires a cause). Therefore, Buti concludes that using rational proofs is actually part of the Quranic method. He then addresses a secondary concern: that his views may contradict some contemporary thinkers. He asserts that correctness, not agreement with others, matters, and that no one after the Prophet is infallible. He ends with a prayer and the date and signature. The footnote references the specific Quranic verses for the proofs mentioned.

Key Terms
العصمة
برهان التمانع
برهان العلة الغائية
برهان بطلان الدور
برهان الرجحان بلا مرجح

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Great scholars are infallible and cannot err.
Correction: Buti asserts that only the Prophet is infallible; any scholar can be mistaken.

Checkpoint
According to Buti, why should one not be concerned if his views contradict some thinkers?
A) Because those thinkers are always wrong
B) Because being correct is more important than agreement
C) Because the Quran says so
D) Because the Prophet said so

Key Takeaway
Human scholars are not infallible; the measure of truth is correctness, not agreement.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hear a respected scholar say something that contradicts your understanding of the Quran and Sunnah, do you instinctively assume you are wrong? How does Buti's statement that no scholar after the Prophet is infallible challenge you to evaluate truth based on evidence rather than personality? What is one step you will take to become more critical in your learning?
?
Buti prays: 'do not entrust me to myself in anything I do, write, or say.' In what area of your life are you most self-reliant—your career, relationships, or religious practice? How can you actively depend on Allah in that area starting today?
?
This lesson says that greatness does not require never erring. Have you ever dismissed a scholar or teacher entirely because of one mistake? How can you maintain respect for their overall contributions while still being truthful about their errors? Commit to one practical change in how you respond to scholarly mistakes.

The Fallibility of Sincere Callers
Author states his stance on errors of reformers and prays for humility.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why even sincere Islamic callers can err and why infallibility is exclusive to the Prophet.

Core Idea
Human fallibility applies to all except the Prophet; intellectual humility is a virtue.

In this concluding passage, the author addresses a common misconception: that great Islamic thinkers or reformers must be correct in everything. He firmly rejects this, asserting that only the Prophet is infallible. This sets a tone of epistemic humility and openness to correction.

Guided Path
1
Read the author's declaration
Read the Arabic passage once, noting the author's strong statement about not caring if his views contradict others as long as they are true.
Notice the phrase 'ولا يعنيني' — this shows intellectual independence.
2
Identify the key condition
Find where the author states the condition for greatness of callers and why it would imply infallibility.
The key phrase: 'فليس شرطاً لعظمة الدعاة... أن لا يخطئوا'
3
Reflect on the implication
Consider why the author includes a personal supplication after this point. How does it reinforce his humility?
The prayer shows he does not claim infallibility for himself.

Source Text

It does not concern me, if my speech is correct, that it comes contrary to what some thinkers or sincere ones see in their call to Islam. For it is not a condition for the greatness of the callers to Allah Almighty and the loftiness of their status and the brightness of their ideas that they do not err in some matter, or that research does not betray them in estimating its true worth from all aspects. If this condition were true, it would mean infallibility indeed. And there is no one after the Messenger of Allah who is described as infallible. That is it. Written in Sha'ban 1390 AH, corresponding to November 1970. Muhammad Sa'id Ramadan al-Buti. = In those cosmic verses in which the divine statement draws attention to the phenomenon of harmony in the creation of components, like His saying: 'And the sun runs to its resting place. That is the decree of the Almighty, the All-Knowing. And the moon, We have measured for it mansions until it returns like an old palm stalk. It is not for the sun to overtake the moon, nor does the night outstrip the day. Commentary
This passage is a concluding statement by the author. He begins by clarifying his intellectual independence: if his words are correct, he does not care if they contradict other thinkers or sincere callers to Islam. He then argues that it is not a condition for the greatness of Islamic callers that they never err in any matter; if that were the case, it would imply infallibility (عصمة), which is exclusive to the Prophet. He then summarizes that these are the ideas he wanted to present in this introduction, and he prays to God for sincerity and reward. After dating and signing the text, he adds a note pointing to Quranic verses that highlight the harmony in creation (such as the sun and moon) and the proof against circular reasoning found in the verse 'Or were they created from nothing...' This note serves as a brief demonstration of how the Quran itself provides evidence for God's existence and the consistency of creation.

Key Terms
عصمة
الدعاة إلى الله

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some believe that great Islamic scholars or reformers are infallible and never make mistakes.
Correction: The author clarifies that only the Prophet is infallible; all others, including sincere callers, can err.

Checkpoint
What does the author say about the possibility of error in Islamic reformers?
A) They are infallible in all matters.
B) It is possible for them to err.
C) Only the Prophet could err.
D) Error is impossible for great callers.

Key Takeaway
Even sincere Islamic callers can err; infallibility is a divine attribute exclusive to prophets.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you implicitly assume that a respected teacher or scholar is always correct in their rulings? How does this passage challenge you to re-evaluate that assumption, and what will you do when you encounter an opinion from them that seems mistaken?
?
The author prays that Allah not entrust him to himself. Have you ever sincerely begged Allah to protect you from your own errors in understanding and practicing Islam? When will you make this your daily prayer?
?
If you were in the author's position—writing a book or giving a talk—would you have the courage to publicly admit that you might be wrong and ask for forgiveness for any mistakes? Does your fear of being seen as imperfect prevent you from that kind of honesty?

Quranic Proofs of Cosmic Harmony and Creation
Author cites Quranic verses on cosmic harmony and the creation argument.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how specific Quranic verses serve as proofs for God's existence through cosmic harmony and the refutation of circular reasoning.

Core Idea
The Quran contains clear rational proofs for God's existence, including design and contingency.

In this passage, the author briefly points to two types of Quranic evidence: the harmony of celestial bodies (sun and moon) and the argument from creation ex nihilo. These verses provide the foundation for classical arguments like the invalidity of preponderance without a preponderant and the refutation of circular reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the Quranic verses cited
Read the Arabic passage carefully, noting how the sun and moon are described in their movements. Then read the second verse about creation.
The verses are from Surah Yasin (36:38-40) and Surah At-Tur (52:35-36).
2
Understand the argument from harmony
Notice the author says these verses highlight 'the phenomenon of harmony in creation'. Think about how the precise orbits of the sun and moon indicate design.
The phrase 'لا الشمس ينبغي لها أن تدرك القمر ولا الليل سابق النهار' shows order.
3
Identify the rational proofs
The author mentions 'the proof of the invalidity of preponderance without a preponderant and the invalidity of circular reasoning'. Connect these to the verse 'أم خلقوا من غير شيء أم هم الخالقون'.
This verse presents a logical dilemma: either created from nothing (no creator) or they create themselves (circular).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Which Quranic argument does the author identify as containing the proof against circular reasoning?

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever genuinely felt the precision of the sun and moon's paths as a personal sign from your Creator, or do you take them for granted? If not, what would it take for you to see them as such starting today?
?
When you consider the verse 'Were they created by nothing, or are they themselves the creators?' (Surah At-Tur 52:35), does it shake you to realize that your own existence is a constant test of where you place the ultimate cause? Will you allow this question to reshape your daily trust in Allah?
?
If you truly internalized that the harmony of the universe is a direct proof of Allah's existence, would you still live as if your life were random? What one habit can you change this week to align your actions with the certainty that there is a Wise Designer?

The Universe and Reason as Signs of God
Author declares the universe as proof of God and reason as the means to perceive it.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the universe and human reason serve as primary proofs for God's existence according to the author.

Core Idea
The universe speaks of God, and reason hears His call.

The author opens his introduction by declaring that the universe itself is filled with signs pointing to its Creator. He then explains that God honored humans with reason so they could perceive these signs. This lesson explores that foundational idea before we move into the importance of creed.

Guided Path
1
Read the opening passage
Read the Arabic text praising Allah and describing the universe as speaking of His signs. Then read the translation to grasp the flow.
2
Identify the role of reason
Notice how the author describes reason as a 'trust' and the tool for understanding the universe's signs. This sets up the rational foundation of faith.
3
Recognize the sequence: universe → reason → faith
The author presents a clear sequence: God created the universe with signs, gave humans reason to perceive them, and sent prophets to remind. See how this builds the case for belief.

مقدمة الطبعة الاولى الحمد الله فاطر السموات والأرض . أنطق الكون بآيات وجوده ، وكشف به عن عظيم سلطانه . خلق الإنسان وشرفه بحمل أمانة العقل ، ليكون الأذن الصاغية لما ينطق به الكون من الآيات ، ثم الوعاء الحاوي لما يتجلى فيه من الدلائل والعظات . أرسل الرسل والأنبياء ، يتوالون مع الزمن، في كل أمة وبقعة ومحيط : أن ذكروا الإنسان بما أوليته من أمانة العقل وما رفعته إليه من شرف السيادة والرياسة في الكون . فليس لائقاً بأشرف مخلوق فيه أن يكون أول كافر أو جاهل بالحق · سبحانه ، جعل العلم بمكنونات خلقه هو السبيل إلى الإيمان بوجوده وجعل مقاليد العلم بذلك كله إلى سلطان العقل وحده ، ليعلم الإنسان بذلك أن لا دين بغير علم ولا علم من دون عقل . والصلاة والسلام على خاتم الأنبياء محمد عليه الصلاة والسلام ، بعث بالدين الذي بعث به من قبله سائر الأنبياء : أن لا إله إلا الله وحده فاعبدوه . وبعث بالشريعة العـامـة الناسخة لما قبله من الشرائع ، صالحة لكل زمان ومكان ، وافية بمصلحة كل فرد وجماعة من الناس وبعد : فإن أساس الإسلام عقيدته ، ومكمن العقيدة فيه إنما هو الإيمان بوجود الله الله عز وجل ووحدانيته . فلا مطمع في تحقيق شيء من أحكام الشريعة الإسلامية إن لم تكن المبادئ الاعتقادية مركزة من قبل ذلك في القلب ، ولا مطمع في ارتكاز شيء من هذه المبادئ فيه إلا بعد الإيمان بوجود الخالق جل جلاله . ولو خلي الإنسان وعقله، دون أن يقوم بينهما أي حاجز من الميول النفسية أو الأغراض الدنيوية أو وسوسة الشياطين من الإنس والجن - لمـا عـاقـه أي شيء عن الإيمان بالله ، ولوجد الكون كله مشحوناً بالبراهين الناطقة بوجوده ، ثم لوجد في القرآن وحده المرقاة إلى أعلى درجات الإيمان واليقين ; فما كان يحتاج عندئذ إلى حجة ونقاش وبرهان وجدال ، ولعاش في غنى عن أن يفكر في أدلة البدهيات ومقدمات الضروريات .
Introduction to the First Edition. Praise be to Allah, the Originator of the heavens and the earth. He made the universe speak with the signs of His existence, and revealed through it His great dominion. He created man and honored him by carrying the trust of reason, to be the listening ear to what the universe speaks of signs, then the container that holds what appears in it of proofs and admonitions. He sent the messengers and prophets, succeeding one another with time, in every nation, place, and environment: that they remind man of the trust of reason that I have given him and the honor of sovereignty and leadership in the universe to which I raised him. So it is not befitting for the most honored creature in it to be the first to disbelieve or be ignorant of the truth. Glory be to Him, He made knowledge of the secrets of His creation the way to belief in His existence, and He placed the keys of all that knowledge solely under the authority of reason, so that man may know thereby that there is no religion without knowledge and no knowledge without reason. And prayers and peace be upon the Seal of the Prophets, Muhammad, peace be upon him; he was sent with the religion with which all the prophets before him were sent: that there is no god but Allah alone, so worship Him. And he was sent with the universal Sharia that abrogates the previous laws, suitable for every time and place, sufficient for the interest of every individual and group of people. After: Indeed, the foundation of Islam is its creed, and the core of the creed is faith in the existence of Allah Almighty and His oneness. So there is no hope of realizing any of the rulings of Islamic Sharia unless the doctrinal principles are first established in the heart, and there is no hope of establishing any of these principles in it except after belief in the existence of the Creator, Majestic is His glory. And if man were left alone with his mind, without any barrier between them of psychological desires, worldly interests, or the whisperings of devils from humans and jinn, nothing would prevent him from believing in Allah, and he would find the whole universe filled with proofs proclaiming His existence, and then he would find in the Qur'an alone the ascent to the highest degrees of faith and certainty; and he would then have no need for argument, discussion, proof, or debate, and he would live in no need to think about evidence of self-evident truths and premises of necessary matters.
Source pages p. 21

Commentary
This passage is the opening of the first edition introduction. It begins with praise to God as the Creator, emphasizing that the universe speaks of His existence. Man is honored with reason as a trust, and prophets are sent to remind him of this. The author then states that knowledge of creation is the path to belief in God, and reason is the tool for attaining such knowledge. He asserts that there is no religion without knowledge and no knowledge without reason. After blessings on the Prophet, he declares that the foundation of Islam is its creed (عقيدة), specifically faith in God's existence and oneness. Without this belief, Islamic rulings cannot be realized. The author then presents a hypothetical: if a person's reason were free from distractions, he would naturally believe in God, seeing proofs in the universe and finding in the Qur'an the highest levels of faith and certainty, requiring no further debate or argument. This establishes the central role of rational belief in the Islamic worldview.

Key Terms
عقل
آيات
وجود

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That faith is purely blind or irrational, requiring no evidence.
Correction: The author argues that the universe provides abundant evidence, and reason is the God-given faculty to perceive it. Faith is thus grounded in knowledge and rational reflection.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what did God place the keys of knowledge under?
A) The prophets
B) Reason alone
C) The Qur'an
D) Religious scholars

Key Takeaway
The universe and reason together form the primary evidence for God's existence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you look at the universe, do you see it as a silent void or as a speaking witness? What prevents you from hearing its testimony?
?
Your reason is a trust from God—are you using it to seek Him, or have you buried it in neglect? What would change if you took that trust seriously today?
?
The prophets came to remind you of what you already know—what reminder are you ignoring right now in your life? Will you act on it today?

Method of Learning
beginner
4 min
Creeds as the Foundation of Islam
Author asserts creed (belief in God) as the foundation of Islam, necessary for Sharia.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the author insists that belief in God (creed) is the indispensable foundation for all Islamic practices and law.

Core Idea
Without belief in God, Islamic law has no ground to stand on.

After establishing the role of reason and the universe, the author turns to a crucial point: the foundation of Islam is its creed, specifically belief in God's existence and oneness. This lesson unpacks that statement and its implications.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on the foundation
Read the Arabic text starting from 'وبعد : فإن أساس الإسلام عقيدته' to 'إلا بعد الإيمان بوجود الخالق جل جلاله'. Then read the translation.
2
Identify the core claim
The author states that the foundation of Islam is its creed (عقيدة), and the core of the creed is faith in God's existence and oneness. This is a hierarchical statement.
3
Analyze the logical priority
Notice the 'so there is no hope' structure: without creed, Sharia rulings cannot be realized; without belief in God, creedal principles cannot be established. This shows creed's foundational role.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Checkpoint
What does the author say is the 'core' of the creed?
A) Belief in angels

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Where in your life have you tried to practice Islam while neglecting to strengthen your belief in God's existence and oneness? What concrete action will you take today to root that belief deeper in your heart?
?
The author insists that without doctrinal principles centered in the heart, there is no hope of truly realizing Sharia. Are you going through the motions of prayer and fasting while your heart remains unconvinced of God's reality? What would change if you genuinely believed His existence?
?
You build your life on something — career, relationships, comfort. But this lesson says belief in God is the only foundation for Islam. Is your belief the foundation of your life, or just a decoration on top of other foundations? What must you tear down to let it become the base?

The Natural Inclination to Believe
Author presents a hypothetical: a distraction-free mind naturally believes in God.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the author's argument that a mind free from distractions naturally arrives at belief in God, finding proof in the universe and the Qur'an.

Core Idea
A clear mind sees God in everything.

The author concludes his introduction with a powerful hypothetical: if a person's reason were free from all barriers—desires, worldly interests, devilish whispers—they would inevitably believe in God. This lesson explores that idea and its implications for faith and certainty.

Guided Path
1
Read the hypothetical scenario
Read the Arabic from 'ولو خلي الإنسان وعقله' to the end. Notice the condition and its result.
2
Identify the barriers
The author lists three barriers: psychological desires, worldly interests, and whisperings of devils. These cloud the natural recognition of God.
3
Understand the result
Without barriers, the person would see the universe full of proofs and find the Qur'an elevating faith to certainty, needing no debate.

Introduction to the First Edition. Praise be to Allah, the Originator of the heavens and the earth. He made the universe speak with the signs of His existence, and revealed through it His great dominion. He created man and honored him by carrying the trust of reason, to be the listening ear to what the universe speaks of signs, then the container that holds what appears in it of proofs and admonitions. He sent the messengers and prophets, succeeding one another with time, in every nation, place, and environment: that they remind man of the trust of reason that I have given him and the honor of sovereignty and leadership in the universe to which I raised him. So it is not befitting for the most honored creature in it to be the first to disbelieve or be ignorant of the truth. Glory be to Him, He made knowledge of the secrets of His creation the way to belief in His existence, and He placed the keys of all that knowledge solely under the authority of reason, so that man may know thereby that there is no religion without knowledge and no knowledge without reason. And prayers and peace be upon the Seal of the Prophets, Muhammad, peace be upon him; he was sent with the religion with which all the prophets before him were sent: that there is no god but Allah alone, so worship Him. And he was sent with the universal Sharia that abrogates the previous laws, suitable for every time and place, sufficient for the interest of every individual and group of people. After: Indeed, the foundation of Islam is its creed, and the core of the creed is faith in the existence of Allah Almighty and His oneness. So there is no hope of realizing any of the rulings of Islamic Sharia unless the doctrinal principles are first established in the heart, and there is no hope of establishing any of these principles in it except after belief in the existence of the Creator, Majestic is His glory. And if man were left alone with his mind, without any barrier between them of psychological desires, worldly interests, or the whisperings of devils from humans and jinn, nothing would prevent him from believing in Allah, and he would find the whole universe filled with proofs proclaiming His existence, and then he would find in the Qur'an alone the ascent to the highest degrees of faith and certainty; and he would then have no need for argument, discussion, proof, or debate, and he would live in no need to think about evidence of self-evident truths and premises of necessary matters.

Commentary
This passage is the opening of the first edition introduction. It begins with praise to God as the Creator, emphasizing that the universe speaks of His existence. Man is honored with reason as a trust, and prophets are sent to remind him of this. The author then states that knowledge of creation is the path to belief in God, and reason is the tool for attaining such knowledge. He asserts that there is no religion without knowledge and no knowledge without reason. After blessings on the Prophet, he declares that the foundation of Islam is its creed (عقيدة), specifically faith in God's existence and oneness. Without this belief, Islamic rulings cannot be realized. The author then presents a hypothetical: if a person's reason were free from distractions, he would naturally believe in God, seeing proofs in the universe and finding in the Qur'an the highest levels of faith and certainty, requiring no further debate or argument. Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That belief in God requires complex philosophical arguments and is unnatural.
Correction: The author argues that belief is natural and intuitive, only obscured by worldly and devilish distractions.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what would a person with an unhindered mind find in the Qur'an?
A) A source of law
B) The ascent to highest degrees of faith and certainty
C) A historical account
D) The need for debate

Key Takeaway
Faith in God is natural and immediate when the mind is free from barriers.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Which barrier among the three mentioned—psychological desires, worldly interests, or whisperings—do you struggle with the most in your own journey of faith? How has it blocked you from seeing the clear proofs of Allah in your life?
?
If you were truly 'left alone with your mind' right now, without any of those barriers, would you find yourself more certain of Allah? What specific step can you take today to remove or weaken the barrier you identified?
?
The passage says that with a clear mind, you would find the Quran alone sufficient to reach the highest degrees of faith and certainty. When you read the Quran, do you approach it with that expectation? What prevents you from experiencing that ascent today?

Method of Learning
beginner
4 min
Knowledge as the Path to Faith
Author declares knowledge of creation as the path to faith and creed as foundation of Islam.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the foundation of Islam is its creed, which is established through knowledge and intellect, and that no religious practice is valid without prior belief in God.

Core Idea
Knowledge of creation, guided by intellect, is the only path to faith in the Creator.

This passage establishes the epistemological foundation of Islamic creed. The author argues that knowledge and intellect are prerequisites for true religion, and that the core of Islam is belief in God's existence and oneness. Without this foundational faith, no religious practice can be meaningful.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing it. Then read the English translation to grasp the author's main argument.
Notice the parallel structure: knowledge leads to faith, intellect governs knowledge, creed is foundation.
2
Identify the three key relationships
Identify how the author connects knowledge to faith, intellect to knowledge, and creed to Islamic practice.
These relationships form the logical backbone of the passage.
3
Reflect on the logical priority
Ask yourself: why must creed come before practice according to the author? What does this imply about the role of intellect in religion?
This connects to the broader theme of rational theology.

سبحانه ، جعل العلم بمكنونات خلقه هو السبيل إلى الإيمان بوجوده وجعل مقاليد العلم بذلك كله إلى سلطان العقل وحده ، ليعلم الإنسان بذلك أن لا دين بغير علم ولا علم من دون عقل . والصلاة والسلام على خاتم الأنبياء محمد عليه الصلاة والسلام ، بعث بالدين الذي بعث به من قبله سائر الأنبياء : أن لا إله إلا الله وحده فاعبدوه . وبعث بالشريعة العـامـة الناسخة لما قبله من الشرائع ، صالحة لكل زمان ومكان ، وافية بمصلحة كل فرد وجماعة من الناس . وبعد : فإن أساس الإسلام عقيدته ، ومكمن العقيدة فيه إنما هو الإيمان بوجود الله عز وجل ووحدانيته . فلا مطمع في تحقيق شيء من أحكام الشريعة الإسلامية إن لم تكن المبادئ الاعتقادية مركزة من قبل ذلك في القلب ، ولا مطمع في ارتكاز شيء من هذه المبادئ فيه إلا بعد الإيمان بوجود الخالق جل جلاله .
Glory be to Him. He made knowledge of the hidden realities of His creation the path to faith in His existence, and He placed the reins of all that knowledge under the authority of the intellect alone, so that man may know thereby that there is no religion without knowledge, and no knowledge without intellect. And peace and blessings be upon the seal of the prophets, Muhammad, peace be upon him; he was sent with the religion with which all the prophets before him were sent: that there is no god but God alone, so worship Him. And he was sent with the universal law (sharīʿa) that abrogates what came before it of laws, suitable for every time and place, sufficient for the welfare of every individual and community of people. To proceed: the foundation of Islam is its creed (ʿaqīda), and the core of the creed in it is only faith in the existence of God Almighty and His oneness. So there is no hope of realizing any of the rulings of Islamic law if the principles of belief are not firmly established in the heart before that, and no hope of any of these principles being established in it except after faith in the existence of the Creator, glorified and exalted be He.
Source pages p. 21

Commentary
This passage is a proclamation of the relationship between knowledge, intellect, and religion. The author states that God has made knowledge of the inner secrets of creation the way to faith in His existence, and He has given the intellect sole authority over that knowledge. The conclusion is a fundamental principle: there is no religion without knowledge, and no knowledge without intellect. This establishes the rational basis of religion. Then the author sends blessings on Prophet Muhammad, stating that he brought the same essential message as previous prophets—monotheism and worship of God alone—and also brought a universal law that abrogates earlier laws, being suitable for all times and places. The author then declares the main thesis: the foundation of Islam is its creed (ʿaqīda), and the core of that creed is faith in God's existence and oneness. No part of Islamic law can be enacted unless creedal principles are firmly rooted in the heart, and such rooting requires prior faith in the existence of the Creator. This passage underscores the absolute necessity of belief in God as the basis for all religious practice.

Correction: This passage insists that religion is grounded in knowledge and intellect: there is no religion without knowledge, and no knowledge without intellect.

What doubts or distractions are you tolerating that undermine it? Are you willing to examine them honestly and seek answers from the very knowledge God has placed within His creation?

Obstacles to Innate Belief: Desires and Doubts
Author describes how desires and worldly attachments obscure the natural inclination to believe in God.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why humans fail to recognize God's existence despite overwhelming evidence, due to internal and external obstacles.

Core Idea
Desires and doubts, not lack of evidence, obscure the natural belief in God.

The author presents a powerful insight: if left to pure reason, everyone would believe in God. But God’s wisdom includes testing us through desires and passions, which create veils over the truth. This lesson explores those obstacles and why theological arguments are necessary.

Guided Path
1
Understand the hypothetical scenario
Read the passage's opening conditional statement. Imagine a person with only intellect and no barriers. The author says such a person would inevitably believe because the universe is full of proofs.
Notice that this scenario is not real, but it shows the natural state.
2
Recognize the obstacles created by God
The author then explains that God, in His wisdom, placed alongside the intellect misleading desires and passions. This makes truth heavy and falsehood easy, leading to fabricated doubts and veils.
Consider why God would allow such obstacles: it's part of testing.
3
See the result: obscuring self-evident truth
These accumulated factors cloud the vision of the self-evident truth (al-ḥaqq al-badīhī). Some people end up viewing it as mere philosophy or imagination.
This shows why we need systematic arguments despite the evidence being clear.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو خلي الإنسان وعقله، دون أن يقوم بينهما أي حاجز من الميول النفسية أو الأغراض الدنيوية أو وسوسة الشياطين من الإنس والجن - لمـا عـاقـه أي شيء عن الإيمان بالله ، ولوجد الكون كله مشحوناً بالبراهين الناطقة بوجوده ، ثم لوجد في القرآن وحده المرقاة إلى أعلى درجات الإيمان واليقين ؛ فما كان يحتاج عندئذ إلى حجة ونقاش وبرهان وجدال ، ولعاش في غنى عن أن يفكر في أدلة البدهيات ومقدمات الضروريات . ولكن الله عز وجل - ( وقد شاءت حكمته أن يبلو الناس بعضهم ببعض ثم يمتحنهم أيهم أحسن عملاً ، ليجزيهم بعد ذلك على ما قد عملوه بالفعل لا على ما قد علمه في سابق غيبه مما سيفعلون ) - جعل إلى جانب العقل المرشد في الإنسان شهوات وأهواء مضللة ، وجعل الإيمان بالحق وأتباعه ثقيلاً على النفس على حين جعل الإيمان بالباطل واتباعه سهلاً خفيفاً عليها . فتولدت بذلك الشبه المصطنعة وتكاثفت الغشاوات المختلقة ، وقام للعصبية في النفوس سلطان أقوى من سلطان العقل الذي في الرؤوس . ثم تجمع من ذلك كله ما عكّر صفاء الرؤية إلى الحق البدهي ، حتى انقلب هذا الحق في ظن بعض الناس إلى فلسفة غيبية وتخيلات وهمية !.
If man were left alone with his intellect, with no barrier between them from psychological inclinations, worldly desires, or the whisperings of devils among humans and jinn – nothing would prevent him from believing in God, and he would find the entire universe filled with proofs speaking of His existence. Then he would find in the Qur'an alone the ascent to the highest levels of faith and certainty. He would then have no need for argument, discussion, proof, or debate, and he would live free from needing to think about evidence for self-evident truths and premises of necessary matters. But God Almighty – and His wisdom willed that He test people by means of one another, then try them as to which of them is best in deed, so that He may reward them afterward for what they actually did, not for what He already knew in His prior unseen knowledge of what they would do – placed alongside the guiding intellect in man misleading desires and passions, and made faith in truth and following it heavy upon the soul, while making faith in falsehood and following it easy and light upon it. Thus, fabricated doubts were generated, concocted veils multiplied, and for partisanship in souls an authority stronger than the authority of the intellect in heads arose. Then from all that accumulated what clouded the clarity of vision toward the self-evident truth, until this truth turned in the opinion of some people into a metaphysical philosophy and imaginary fantasies!.
Source pages p. 21

Commentary
This passage is an analysis of why people fail to believe despite the evidence. The author presents a conditional scenario: if man were left with only his intellect and no barriers, he would inevitably believe, because the universe is filled with proofs and the Qur'an guides to certainty. He would not need extra arguments. However, God's wisdom includes testing people through each other and through trials, so He placed alongside the intellect misleading desires and passions. Faith in truth is made heavy on the soul, while faith in falsehood is made easy. This results in fabricated doubts, accumulated veils, and the dominance of partisanship over intellect. Consequently, the clear truth becomes obscured, and some people come to view it as mere metaphysical speculation and imaginary fantasies. The passage explains the epistemological and psychological obstacles to belief, justifying the need for systematic theological argumentation despite the self-evident nature of God's existence.

الحق البدهي
الوسوسة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think belief in God is purely voluntary and that people disbelieve simply because they choose to.
Correction: The passage shows that internal factors (desires, passions) and external factors (whisperings, partisanship) can hinder the natural recognition of truth, making disbelief not simply a matter of choice but of obstacles.

Checkpoint

A) Because the Qur'an requires scholarly interpretation.
B) Because God has placed misleading desires and passions alongside the intellect, creating obstacles.
C) Because the intellect alone is insufficient to understand the universe.
D) Because the universe's proofs are hidden and require scientists to uncover them.

Key Takeaway
The natural inclination to believe in God can be obscured by desires, passions, and doubts, requiring active seeking of truth despite obstacles.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

?
The passage says that following truth is heavy upon the soul while falsehood is easy. Where in your life have you chosen the easy path of falsehood over the heavy truth? How will you start choosing the heavy path this week?
?
If left alone with your intellect, nothing would prevent you from believing. Yet you are not left alone—your heart is full of desires and partisanship. What specific worldly desire or loyalty is currently preventing you from submitting fully to the truth, and what will you sacrifice to overcome it?

Method of Learning

The Necessity of Treating Necessary Truths as Theoretical
Author prescribes method for treating necessary truths as theoretical

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why a believer must treat the necessary truth of God's existence as a theoretical matter, subjecting all possible objections to scientific examination with a free intellect.

Core Idea
Self-evident truths must be proven when doubts distort them.

In this passage, the author provides a methodological justification for the entire kalam project. He explains that because doubts and uncertainties have been raised against the necessary truth of God's existence, the believing researcher cannot simply rely on self-evidence. Instead, he must imagine all possible objections, examine them rigorously, and expose their falsity, leading to clear outcomes.

Guided Path
1
Understand the necessity
Read why the author says that a necessary truth must be given the account of theoretical matters. Note the reason: because doubts have been raised.
This is the core methodological claim.
2
Identify the researcher's task
Find the steps the researcher must take: imagine all causes of doubt, place them in the balance of scientific research, and direct free intellect upon them.
The process is active and rigorous.
3
Recognize the two outcomes
Notice the two possible results once falseness is uncovered: either opponents cease their doubts or they persist, revealing their intentions.
This shows the method's purpose: to clarify truth and reveal motives.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
من أجل ذلك ، كان لا بد من أن يُحسب لهذه الحقيقة الضرورية حساب المسائل النظرية . بأن يتخيل الباحث ) مهما كان مؤمناً مستيقناً ببديهة عقله ( كل ما يمكن أن يثار حولها من أسباب الشبه والشكوك ، فيضعها ، بكل جد ، في ميزان البحث العلمي ، ثم يسلط عليها أشعة العقل المتدبر الحر، حتى إذا انكشف زيفها ، تولدت من ذلك إحدى نتيجتين : إما أن يكف دعاتها عن احتضانها والمقارعة بها فيتجلى صدق بحثهم وحرية عقولهم ، وإما أن يستمروا في العكوف عليها والدعوة إليها فيتجلى بذلك زيف مقاصدهم وتنكشف عبودية أفكارهم . ولا ينبغي أن يضيق الباحث المؤمن ذرعاً ، من أجل أنه إنما يبرهن على البدهيات التي لا تحتاج - بإجماع العقلاء - إلى براهين ؛ لأن هذه البدهية بالذات قد انقلبت في خيال كثير من الناس إلى نظريات خاضعة للبحث والفكر والنقاش ، لما قلنا من أنه أساس سائر التكليفات الإلهية للبشر . ولو كان أساس هذه التكليفات ضرورة الإيمان بوجود الشمس الساطعة في كبد السماء ، لقام في الناس من ينكرها ويتمارى فيها ، ولقام من ذلك حجاب كثيف بينها وبين أوهام كثير من الناس . فمن أجل ذلك ألف أسلافنا الله المطولات والمختصرات المختلفة في ذكر الأدلة والبراهين العلمية على وجود الله ، ورضوا أن ينزلوا بعقولهم إلى مستوى من قد يتخيل وجود الله نظرية عويصة تحتاج إلى كثير من المقدمات والشروح ، فنثروا هذه المقدمات والشروح كلها واستحضروا لذلك موازين الفكر العقلي المطلق وموازين الفلسفة اليونانية
Because of that, it became necessary that this necessary truth (ḥaqīqa ḍarūriyya) be given the account of theoretical matters: that the researcher – no matter how much he is a believer, certain by the intuitive perception of his intellect – should imagine all the causes of doubts and uncertainties that could be raised about it, place them, with all seriousness, in the balance of scientific research, then direct upon them the rays of the free, contemplative intellect; until when their falseness is uncovered, one of two results arises: either their advocates cease embracing and disputing with them, thus the sincerity of their research and the freedom of their minds becomes evident; or they persist in clinging to them and calling to them, thus the falseness of their intentions becomes evident and the bondage of their ideas is exposed. The believing researcher should not be distressed because he is proving self-evident matters that – by consensus of the rational people – do not need proofs; because this particular self-evident truth has turned in the imagination of many people into theories subject to research, thought, and debate, because, as we said, it is the foundation of all divine obligations for humans. And if the foundation of these obligations were the necessity of believing in the existence of the sun shining in the middle of the sky, there would arise among people those who deny it and argue about it, and a thick veil would arise between it and the imaginations of many people. For that reason, our predecessors – may God have mercy on them – authored lengthy and abridged works presenting scientific proofs and evidences for the existence of God, and they consented to descend with their intellects to the level of those who might imagine that God's existence is a complex theory requiring many premises and explanations. So they presented all these premises and explanations and brought to bear for that the balances of pure rational thought and the balances of Greek philosophy.
Source pages p. 22

Commentary
This passage provides the methodological justification for treating the self-evident truth of God's existence as a theoretical problem. The author argues that because doubts and confusions have obscured this truth, the believer must adopt the approach of imagining all possible objections, examining them seriously with free intellect, and exposing their falsity. Two outcomes are possible: either the opponents will abandon their doubts (showing their sincerity) or persist (showing their bad faith). The author reassures the believer not to be troubled by proving what is self-evident, because this particular truth has become theoretical in many people's minds due to its foundational role for all obligations. Analogously, even something as clear as the sun would be denied if it were the foundation. For this reason, Islamic scholars throughout history wrote extensive and concise works providing rational and scientific proofs for God's existence, descending to the level of those who treat it as a complex theory, using both pure rational thought and Greek philosophical frameworks. This passage legitimizes the entire kalam project as a necessary response to doubt and skepticism.

Key Terms
الحقيقة الضرورية
المسائل النظرية
الشبه
الشكوك
البحث العلمي
العقل المتدبر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: A believer should never subject the truth of God's existence to theoretical examination because it is self-evident.
Correction: The author argues that because doubts have been raised, it is necessary to treat it theoretically, examining objections with scientific rigor, to expose falsity and reveal motives.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is one of the two possible outcomes when the falseness of doubts is uncovered?
A) The researcher abandons his faith.
B) The opponents cease their objections, showing sincerity.
C) The doubts become stronger.
D) The researcher must accept the doubts.

Key Takeaway
When necessary truths are obscured by doubt, they must be treated as theoretical and examined with scientific rigor to expose falsity and reveal intentions.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever avoided engaging with a doubt about your faith because you feared it would weaken your certainty? How does this lesson challenge that avoidance and what would it look like for you to put that doubt 'in the balance of scientific research'?
?
When you encounter an objection to a belief you hold as self-evident, do you instinctively dismiss it or do you treat it as a theoretical matter worthy of serious investigation? What does your usual reaction reveal about your intellectual sincerity?
?
If your response to a skeptic's doubt is to never examine it, are you truly certain or just comfortable? What would it cost you to follow the author's method and shine the light of free intellect on that doubt—and what might you gain?

Reassurance and the Precedent of Scholars
Author reassures and cites precedent for using rational proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why proving self-evident truths is not a weakness, and how the example of predecessors justifies using rational and philosophical arguments.

Core Idea
Proving the obvious is necessary when it is foundational.

The author addresses the concern a believer might have about proving something so self-evident. He reassures by highlighting the foundational importance of God's existence for all obligations and uses an analogy of the sun. He then invokes the example of earlier scholars who wrote extensive works and even used Greek philosophy, setting a precedent for the use of rational arguments.

Guided Path
1
Read the reassurance
Pay attention to why the author says the believer should not be distressed about proving self-evident matters.
The reason is the foundational role of this truth.
2
Examine the analogy
Consider the hypothetical example of the sun: if belief in its existence were the foundation, even it would be denied.
This shows how essential truths can be doubted when they are foundational.
3
Learn from the predecessors
Notice that the author cites the scholars who wrote lengthy and abridged works, using rational and Greek philosophical arguments.
This historical example legitimizes the use of philosophical reasoning.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever felt embarrassed or hesitant to use rational arguments for God's existence, thinking it shows weak faith? How does the author's reassurance address that feeling? What will you do the next time you are in a discussion where faith is challenged?
?
The author says the foundation of all divine obligations is belief in God. If that foundation is doubted, everything else is at risk. In your own life, do you treat belief in God as a settled foundation, or do you sometimes let doubts shake you? What concrete step can you take to strengthen your conviction?
?
The early scholars humbled themselves to engage with doubters using rational and philosophical tools. Are you willing to descend from the comfort of certainty to engage with those who are confused about God's existence? What is one thing you can learn (a proof, a philosophical argument) this week to be better equipped?

How Desires and Partisan Loyalties Obscure Necessary Truth
Buti enumerates the causes of doubt about necessary truths from human desires and partisanship.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why necessary truths can become obscured by human desires, passions, and partisanship, as explained by Buti.

Core Idea
Desires and partisanship can cloud even the most obvious truths.

Buti begins by explaining a profound challenge to theological knowledge: even necessary truths can become objects of doubt. He traces this to the human condition, where Allah placed alongside reason misleading desires and passions. This passage reveals the psychological and sociological factors that lead people to reject clear truths.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic once without analysis, then the translation to grasp the flow.
2
Identify the factors
Notice how Buti lists the causes: desires, partisanship, ease of falsehood, strengthening of bias.
The sequence is important.
3
Reflect on the outcome
See how these factors cumulatively cloud necessary truth, turning it into a mere philosophy for some.
This explains why many reject obvious truths.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولكن الله عز وجل - ( وقد شاءت حكمته أن يبلو الناس بعضهم ببعض ثم يمتحنهم أيهم أحسن عملاً ، ليجزيهم بعد ذلك على ما قد عملوه بالفعل لا على ما قد علمه في سابق غيبه مما سيفعلون ) - جعل إلى جانب العقل المرشد في الإنسان شهوات وأهواء مضللة ، وجعل الإيمان بالحق وأتباعه ثقيلاً على النفس على حين جعل الإيمان بالباطل واتباعه سهلاً خفيفاً عليها فنتولدت بذلك الشبه المصطنعة وتكاثفت الغشاوات المختلقة ، وقام للعصبية في النفوس سلطان أقوى من سلطان العقل الذي في الرؤوس . ثم تجمع من ذلك كله ما عكّر صفاء الرؤية إلى الحق البدهي ، حتى انقلب هذا الحق في ظن بعض الناس إلى فلسفة غيبية وتخيلات وهمية !.
But Allah the Mighty and Majestic – and His wisdom willed to test people by means of each other, then to try them which of them is best in deed, so that He may recompense them afterwards for what they have actually done, not for what He knew in His prior knowledge that they would do – placed alongside the guiding intellect in man misleading desires and passions, and made belief in truth and following it heavy upon the soul, while making belief in falsehood and following it easy and light upon it. Thus fabricated doubts were produced and artificial veils thickened, and partisanship gained in souls a dominion stronger than the dominion of the intellect in heads. Then from all that accumulated what clouded the clarity of vision to the necessary truth, until this truth turned in the opinion of some people into a metaphysical philosophy and imaginary fantasies!
Source pages p. 22

Commentary
This passage is an explanation of why necessary truths become objects of doubt. Buti describes God's test through giving humans both reason and desires. He states that God made following truth heavy and following falsehood easy, leading to fabricated doubts and partisanship overcoming reason. Consequently, the clear necessary truth is clouded and perceived by some as a complex philosophical theory. The author follows the sequence: God's wisdom, then the placement of desires, the effect on belief, the production of doubts, the domination of partisanship, and finally the obscuring of truth.

حق بدهي

Misconception: Necessary truths are self-evident and cannot be doubted by anyone.
Correction: Buti explains that even necessary truths can be obscured by desires, passions, and partisanship, causing some to doubt or reinterpret them.

Checkpoint
According to the author, what made belief in truth heavy and belief in falsehood easy?
A) The intellect
B) Desires and passions
C) Partisanship
D) God's prior knowledge

Key Takeaway
Desires, passions, and partisanship can cloud even the most obvious truths, turning them into mere opinions.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Consider a time when you found it easy to accept a falsehood because it aligned with your desires. What did that reveal about the state of your heart, and what truth were you avoiding? Will you now actively seek that truth even if it feels heavy?
?
The passage says partisanship has a stronger dominion than intellect. In what area of your life—whether religious, political, or social—are you letting group loyalty override clear evidence? Are you willing to break that allegiance for the sake of truth?
?
You may believe in the truth of Islam, but do you actually feel the weight of following it? If belief in truth feels heavy to you, ask yourself: what desires have made falsehood feel light? What will you change today to make truth easier for your soul?

Why Necessary Truths Need Theoretical Defense
Buti presents a methodological requirement for defending necessary truths and enumerates two results.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why necessary truths must be treated as theoretical issues and the two possible outcomes of such treatment.

Core Idea
Even self-evident truths need intellectual defense against doubt.

Buti argues that in a world where doubts arise about even the most obvious realities, believers cannot simply rely on intuitive certainty. They must engage with objections seriously, treating necessary truths as if they were theoretical questions. This passage lays out the method and the two possible results.

Guided Path
1
Understand the context
Recognize that necessary truths are being doubted, requiring a response.
2
Grasp the method
The researcher must imagine all possible doubts, examine them scientifically, and use free reflection.
3
Identify the two outcomes
Once falsehood is exposed, advocates either desist (showing sincerity) or persist (showing falsehood).
4
Reflect on the importance
This method defends truth and reveals the true motives of opponents.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
من أجل ذلك ، كان لا بد من أن يُحسب لهذه الحقيقة الضرورية حساب المسائل النظرية . بأن يتخيل الباحث ( مهما كان مؤمناً مستيقناً ببديهة عقله ) كل ما يمكن أن يثار حولها من أسباب الشبه والشكوك ، فيضعها ، بكل جد ، في ميزان البحث العلمي ، ثم يسلط عليها أشعة العقل المتدبر الحر، حتى إذا انكشف زيفها ، تولدت من ذلك إحدى نتيجتين : إما أن يكف دعاتها عن احتضانها والمقارعة بها فيتجلى صدق بحثهم وحرية عقولهم ، وإما أن يستمروا في العكوف عليها والدعوة إليها فيتجلى بذلك زيف مقاصدهم وتنكشف عبودية أفكارهم
For that reason, it was necessary that this necessary truth be given the status of theoretical issues: that the researcher – no matter how believing and certain he may be by the intuition of his intellect – imagine all the causes of doubts and suspicions that can be raised about it, then place them, in all seriousness, in the scale of scientific research, then direct upon them the rays of the free, reflective intellect, until when their falsehood is exposed, one of two results is produced: either its advocates desist from embracing and arguing with them, thus revealing the sincerity of their research and freedom of their minds, or they continue to cling to them and call to them, thus revealing the falsehood of their objectives and exposing the servitude of their thoughts.
Source pages p. 22

Commentary
This passage is a methodological argument. Buti asserts that because necessary truths have become subject to doubt, they must be treated as theoretical problems. He prescribes a method: the researcher, regardless of personal certainty, must anticipate all possible doubts, examine them scientifically, and use free reflection. The outcome will be one of two: either the doubters abandon their position (proving their sincerity) or they persist (proving their dishonesty). The author follows a logical sequence: reason (min ajl dhalika), requirement (la budda), method (bi-an yatakhayyal...), and results (imma... wa imma...).

Key Terms
حقيقة ضرورية
مسائل نظرية
شبه
شكوك
عقل متدبر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Necessary truths are self-evident and do not need to be argued or defended.
Correction: Buti argues that because doubts have been raised, they must be treated as theoretical issues and subjected to rigorous examination.

Checkpoint
What are the two possible outcomes after the researcher exposes the falsehood of doubts?
A) The doubts disappear or become stronger
B) The advocates desist or continue
C) The researcher becomes more certain or doubtful
D) The truth becomes easier or harder

Key Takeaway
Believers must treat necessary truths as theoretical issues and be prepared for either outcome, which reveals the character of the opponents.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hold a truth as certain, do you actively seek out and examine the strongest doubts against it, or do you avoid them? What does your answer reveal about your intellectual freedom?
?
If you discovered that a belief you cherish could not survive rigorous intellectual scrutiny, would you abandon it or cling to it? What would your choice say about your sincerity?
?
Are you willing to treat your most deeply held convictions as theoretical, exposing them to the 'rays of the free reflective intellect'? What one step will you take today to practice this method in your own heart?

Reassurance on Proving Self-Evident Truths
Buti reassures the believer to prove self-evident truths.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why proving self-evident truths is necessary and not a cause for distress.

Core Idea
Self-evident truths need proof when doubters arise.

Buti addresses the believing researcher who may feel uneasy proving obvious truths. He explains that these truths have become obscured in many people's minds, turning into theories that require proof. The sun example illustrates how even the most obvious can be denied.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the tone: Buti is reassuring.
2
Identify the main point
Buti says the believing researcher should not be distressed. Why? Because the self-evident truth has become doubted.
3
Understand the sun analogy
He uses the example of the sun. Even something so obvious can be denied, so proof is needed.
This illustrates how doubt can arise.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا ينبغي أن يضيق الباحث المؤمن ذرعاً ، من أجل أنه إنما يبرهن على البدهيات التي لا تحتاج - بإجماع العقلاء - إلى براهين ؛ لأن هذه البدهية بالذات قد انقلبت في خيال كثير من الناس إلى نظريات خاضعة للبحث والفكر والنقاش ، لما قلنا من أنه أساس سائر التكليفات الإلهية للبشر . ولو كان أساس هذه التكليفات ضرورة الإيمان بوجود الشمس الساطعة في كبد السماء ، لقام في الناس من ينكرها ويتمارى فيها ، ولقام من ذلك حجاب كثيف بينها وبين أوهام كثير من الناس . فمن أجل ذلك ألف أسلافنا الله رحمهم المطولات والمختصرات المختلفة في ذكر الأدلة والبراهين العلمية على وجود الله ، ورضوا أن ينزلوا بعقولهم إلى مستوى من قد يتخيل وجود الله نظرية عويصة تحتاج إلى كثير من المقدمات والشروح ، فنثروا هذه المقدمات والشروح كلها واستحضروا لذلك موازين الفكر العقلي المطلق وموازين الفلسفة اليونانية ، حتى لا يتورك باحث مغرض يصطنع الشبه اصطناعاً على أحد الميزانين فيقارع به ويحتكم إليه . ولولا هؤلاء المغرضون والمتحذلقون ، لوسع المسلمين ما وسع الصحابة من قبلهم من بداهة الفكر وحرية العقل ودلائل القرآن والكون
And it should not distress the believing researcher that he is proving self-evident truths which – by consensus of the rational – do not need proofs; because this self-evident truth itself has turned in the imagination of many people into theories subject to research, thought, and debate, due to what we said that it is the basis of all divine obligations for humans. If the basis of these obligations were the necessity of believing in the existence of the sun shining in the middle of the sky, there would arise among people those who deny it and dispute about it, and a thick veil would arise from that between it and the illusions of many people. For that reason, our predecessors – may God have mercy on them – authored long and abridged works on the scientific proofs for the existence of God, and were content to descend with their intellects to the level of one who imagines God's existence as a complex theory needing many premises and explanations, so they laid out all these premises and explanations and summoned for that the scales of absolute rational thought and the scales of Greek philosophy, so that no biased researcher who artificially fabricates doubts can rely on either scale and argue with it and appeal to it. And were it not for these biased and pedantic people, the Muslims would have sufficed with what sufficed the Companions before them of intuitive thought, freedom of intellect, and the evidences of the Qur'an and the universe.
Source pages p. 22

Commentary
This passage is both a reassurance and a historical justification. Buti first addresses the believing researcher, telling him not to be distressed by proving self-evident truths, because these truths have become doubted due to human factors. He uses a hypothetical example of the sun to show that even obvious truths can be denied. Then he explains why early scholars (aslafuna) wrote extensive works: they descended to the level of those who imagine God's existence as a complex theory, and they used both rational and Greek philosophical scales to preempt biased arguers. He concludes that without such biased people, simple intuitive faith would have sufficed, as it did for the Companions.

Key Terms
بدهيات
تكليفات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Buti, why should the believing researcher not be distressed?
A) Because proofs are unnecessary
B) Because self-evident truths have become doubted by many
C) Because the sun is a clear example
D) Because early scholars wrote many books

Key Takeaway
Proving self-evident truths is necessary because they have become doubted by many.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever felt hesitant to defend your belief in Allah because it seemed too obvious to need proof? How does Buti's reassurance that even self-evident truths are doubted address that fear in your own heart?
?
Think of a specific moment when you doubted something fundamental about your faith—perhaps God's wisdom, mercy, or existence. Did you try to prove it to yourself? What was the result?
?
If the basis of all divine obligations were as obvious as the sun, would you still sometimes doubt it? What does that tell you about the nature of your own faith and the need for continual conviction?

The Legacy of Early Theologians
Buti explains the necessity of early scholars' extensive proofs using reason and philosophy.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the early scholars (aslaf) wrote long and abridged works using reason and Greek philosophy to prove God's existence.

Core Idea
Early scholars used comprehensive proofs to preempt doubters.

Buti explains the historical context behind the extensive theological works of the early scholars. They descended to the level of those who saw God's existence as complex theory, using both rational and Greek philosophical tools to counter fabricators of doubt.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation. This part explains why early scholars wrote many works.
2
Find the reason
The reason is given after 'فمن أجل ذلك'. They authored long and short books on proofs.
3
Understand the method
They 'descended' to the level of those who saw God's existence as complex, and used scales of rational thought and Greek philosophy.
This shows their thoroughness.
4
Note the purpose
To prevent biased researchers from fabricating doubts and using those scales against them.
5
Reflect on the conclusion
Without such troublemakers, simple intuitive faith would have sufficed, as it did for the Companions.
